  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d59ae0e7-a5b3-401d-8518-11e5bdf5de04'
      });

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634441083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17033539037853738477">When I saw Sweet's latest novel had to do with zombies, I groaned a little. I mean lately there is nothing but zombies & vampires everywhere you look. I like both subjects, but still. Ya know? I should not have worried. This book is outstanding. I'll go so far to say it may be my all time favorite on the subject of zombies. <br/><br/>The writing is crisp & tight; I felt for each and every character, even the 'new' breed of zombies; Speaking of the 'new breed' of zombies: Brilliant! Just brilliant. Excelle</span>
  <span id="freeText17033539037853738477" style="display:none">When I saw Sweet's latest novel had to do with zombies, I groaned a little. I mean lately there is nothing but zombies &amp; vampires everywhere you look. I like both subjects, but still. Ya know? I should not have worried. This book is outstanding. I'll go so far to say it may be my all time favorite on the subject of zombies. <br /><br />The writing is crisp &amp; tight; I felt for each and every character, even the 'new' breed of zombies; Speaking of the 'new breed' of zombies: Brilliant! Just brilliant. Excellent premise, and one I had not personally ever come across. Joseph Sweet needs to be a household name. Seriously.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2029520-randy-harmelink?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer915149461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16834112634695505868">I liked the concept of the book, but hated the execution of it. Although it has a somewhat unique bent on zombies, the book never engaged me in either the story or the characters. At times, I found the writing awkward, having to go back and reread a paragraph, even a page, to understand what the author was writing. <br/><br/>I won't be continuing in the series, even though I am curious where it will end up.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6757737873329559623">YES!! This is the zombie book I was looking for! Man, there's a lot of crap horror out there. I've been weeding through trying to find something that fills my desire to watch zombie movies and The Walking Dead but in book form. This did it, to a T. I'd call this "smart horror", if such thing exists. The plot is no more believable than any other zombie story, BUT it's well-written and takes zombies to a whole new level with a as-plausable-as-zombie-stories-can-be plot line. I love that this is wr</span>
  <span id="freeText6757737873329559623" style="display:none">YES!! This is the zombie book I was looking for! Man, there's a lot of crap horror out there. I've been weeding through trying to find something that fills my desire to watch zombie movies and The Walking Dead but in book form. This did it, to a T. I'd call this "smart horror", if such thing exists. The plot is no more believable than any other zombie story, BUT it's well-written and takes zombies to a whole new level with a as-plausable-as-zombie-stories-can-be plot line. I love that this is written from a variety of view-points in easy-to-digest chapters. It kept me engaged and my only regret is I wish I was longer. I can't wait for the next book in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6757737873329559623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pheebz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pheebz" href="/user/show/32536934-pheebz">Pheebz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818854462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6156813213698655764">Requiem for Humanity By Joseph Sweet<br/>Such a good book. This was the second book I had read of Mr. Sweet. The first being a novella The Drawer which I will be posting a review shortly. <br/>Requiem was a unique take in this genre. The common thread through the many groups of survivors had written down the events that had pertained to their group, observations and surviving. Some even left warnings for other survivors of things they had witnessed first hand and discoveries made along the way to survival</span>
  <span id="freeText6156813213698655764" style="display:none">Requiem for Humanity By Joseph Sweet<br />Such a good book. This was the second book I had read of Mr. Sweet. The first being a novella The Drawer which I will be posting a review shortly. <br />Requiem was a unique take in this genre. The common thread through the many groups of survivors had written down the events that had pertained to their group, observations and surviving. Some even left warnings for other survivors of things they had witnessed first hand and discoveries made along the way to survival. <br />It all started with a group finding a journal of a survivor's account and timeline of events as she witnessed them. The finder of the journal thought that it was a good idea to continue on. They would write the account of what had become of their lives in the group they were in. None of these various groups knew if there were other survivors out there after years of the undead walking the earth, but when they were done they would each leave the journal in a public place along with other survivor's journals they found, in hopes that the discoveries made would help others to survive .<br />Up till the Zombie apocalypse happened most only knew what they had read in books or seen in the movies. If that were that lucky to have been a consumer of zombie fiction at all. <br />Two years after the outbreak the Zombies were not what they once were slow, brain dead and hungry . They are now cunning, resourceful and able to use tools. It appears the smart zombies started from a failed attempt by the C.E.L.L to find a cure and the experiments they were doing on any Survivors they came across.<br />Penelope was saved from the C.E.L.L.'s men who were mistaken for the Military. by Ed or if you want the full name, Eduardo Enrique Luiz. However, things changed from that point on for both Penelope &amp; Ed as well as for Zombie kind. Pick up this book, you won't be sorry, there is a second book in this series out now also you'll want to read as well.<br />Mr. Sweet did a great job creating a world with well-rounded characters with depth.<br />I look forward to reading more by this Author. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6156813213698655764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Qml0TBZxnWR4oixgdGR6V3GB8ZIOZl1Dd53xMQl0Z2Cgo4+aphCkXFCEPXlGQsCBw9tbjRbwgCYjtoJqIfBp+Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KrLBvuBpYrsokdSG113lwDG+MHWd3BP3fbKzFPkDIY/IeDpoUAhbgwC3xZ/le18Wg+SaaoVKzpIpmcBP0YcvFg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10474578684436025071">Joseph Sweet was born October 31, 1976, and has been writing seriously since the age of sixteen. He currently lives in the upstate NY community of Watertown. He is author of the series of novels, "The Damnation Chronicles" and "Last Days," and a steadily growing number of short stories. You can read more about him, as well as information on other projects, at his website. <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.josephsweet.co.nr'>http://www.josephsweet.co</a></span>

a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
